IR/PS Dean to Take on New Role 
Richard Feinberg. the dean of UCSD's Graduate 

School of International Relations and PaCifiC Sludles 
(IR/PS). Will step down as dean In order to become 
director of tile unlverslty's ASia PaCifiC Economic 
Cooperation (APEC ) Studies Center. Feinberg Will also 
serve as a specIal adVisor to the chancellor for PaC ifiC 
RIIll affairs . 

The APEC Studies Center, based at IRI PS , IS a fed· 
erally·funded center dedicated to promoting research . 
scholarly exchange and public education on subjects 
of Interest to 19 PaCifiC Rim APECmember countries. 

Feinberg Will remain all active member of the 
IRI PS faculty and will develop a plan for Increasi ng 
UCSD's links In the PaCifiC Rim region and the Inter· 
national commullily at large, 

Miles Kahler will serve as acting dean for IRIPS 
dUrlilg the search for a new. permanent dean . 

Rehabilitation Program Offers 
Transportation Alternative 

The [mployee Rehabilitation Program Will prOVide 
staff, faculty and vIsitors With medical Impairments 
the use of a golf cart to drive while on campus, 

Th e golf cart IS kept III the Torrry Pilles 
Center/South garage. located Just off campus at 
10280 N. Torrey Pines Road For more IIlformatlon. 
call the Employee Rehabilitation Program at 5346744 
or 534·6743 

In addition to tile goll cart. UCSD community mem 
bers With medical Impall mems can apply for a handl 
capped·accesslble parklllg placard from the state 
Department of Motor Vehicles. 

SIO Scientist Ramanathan 
Awarded Environmental Prize 

Veerabhadran Ramanathan. a professor of atmos· 
phenc sCiences and director of the Scnpps Institution 
of Oceanography's Center for Clouds . Chemistry and 
Climate. has been awarded the 1997 Volvo 
EnVIronment Prize for hiS work In studying the green 
house effect. 

Ramanathan was Cited for uncovering the role that 
clouds and water vapor play In distributing energy In 
the earth 's climate system. HIS work also showed that 
the warming effect of so-called greenhouse gases -
slIch as methane, nitrous OXide, CFCs and tropos· 
pherlc ozone - was almost equaled by carbon dlox 
Ide. 

The Volvo EnVIronment Prize was Instituted In 1988 
to promote research and development across the 
enVIronmental spectrum. 

Wolfe Chosen to Direct UCSD 
Space Sciences Center 

Arthur M. Wolfe has been apPOinted director of the 
Center for AstrophYSICS and Space SCiences (CASS). 

Wolfe . a professor of phYSICS and holder of the 
endowed Chancellor's ASSOCiates Chair IV. succeeds 
Lawrence E. Peterson. Peterson has served as CASS 
director slllce 1988. 

Before JOtnlllg UCSD. Wolfe was a member of the 
phYSICS and astronomy faculty of the UniverSity of 
Pittsburgh for 17 years. He has also been a research 
associate With the Cambridge University Institute of 
Theoretical Astronomy.

THE LAW AND SOCIETY PROGRAM offers an interdiSCiplinary minor that 
emphasizes Ihe complexl ly and interrelationship of legal, social, and 
ethical Issues In their historical contexts. Humanities, natural science and 
SOCial science majors bene fit from thiS program by learning how to analyze 
and understand the legal Implications and rami fications of policy and 
deCISion making In their fields. resgonsibilily 

Fall Quarter Course Offerings: 
Economics 118A - Law and Economics 
LinguisticslGeneral176 - The Language of Persuasion 
Political Science 1 04A - The Supreme Court and the Constitution 
Political Science 104L - Positive Political Theory of Law 
Psychology 162 - Psychology and the Law 
Sociology/B 142 - Social Deviance 
Sociology/C 140 - Sociology of Law

Theirs and Yours. 
Join AmeriCorps, the domestic Peace Corps. By tutoring kids, restoring streams 
and parks, building playgrounds, helping communities hit by disasters, serving in a 
health clinic, or meeting other important needs, you'll help others succeed . 
When you join AmeriCorps for one year, you get: 

* A living allowance and health care 
* .Skills for your future 
* Deferment of qualified student loans 
* Almost $5,000 for education

products for the househOld. cosmetiC, personal care and pharmaceulicallndustnes. 
In add Ilion to products for Ihe general populatIon, companies are now formulallng 
products for people of different ethniC backgrounds and skin types ,

CSRlls currently recruIting a Japanese panel to lest a newly deSigned senSitIve 
skin product hne . We need your assIstance In developing thIS unIque panel. 

Panelists are paid for their partICipation The test consists of applYing a patch Similar 
to an adhesive bandage to the upper arm. The patch stays in place for 24 hours, 
IS removed, the skin evaluated and the patch reapplied . Discomfort IS minImal, 
equal 10 haVing a piece of tape removed from the skin. 

Do you qualify?

• Must be a minimum of 18 years of age 
• Must be in good physical health (no pregnant or 

lactating women) 
• Must not have a known allergy to tape 
• Must be willing to participate in pre-screening for 

sensitive skin

Cheap Textbooks!! 
Where??? 

Well the General Store Co-oJ) of 
course. We have all the books you need for: 
Ames, Biology, Chem, CSE, ECE, 
Math, PhYSics, Psych, and a few 

othersHJ 
All these great classes and at prices that are guaranteed to be 
lower than the bookstore. What the HELL? 

How con they do it? 
Well, the General Store Co-op is a non-profit store run completely 
by students , for the students, This allows us to offer a lower overhead and give 
the students less of a mark up. Come on in and see us, we love you and we need 
your support if we are going to be able to continue giving the best book deals this 
side of the Pecos. We are located in the old student center near Soft Reserves. 

Main Phone 534-3932 and Special Textbook line 534-8840

Transfer to Transit U. 

Make the switch to transit and save on your commute and parking 
costs. Take a break from traffic and get some extra time to study. 
UCSD students ride free In ''the zone" by showing the driver 
the yellow bus sticker on your UCSD ID~ With a valid student 10, 
you'll also receive a $10 discount on a monthly bus and trolley 

pass. Use it to ride as many buses and trolleys as you want all month 
long. You've got enough on your mind. Like classes, tests, papers, 
jobs, your love life (or lack of one), and where you're going in life. 
So don't hassle about transportation or how you're going to get there. 

Transfer to Transit U. It's a cool school of thought. 

San Diego Transit ltd, San Diego Trolley 
-, ' . 

The routes to know to get where you want to go. 
150 - Express bus takes you Downtown, Horton Plaza, 
Greyhound bus station from VA Hospital at peak hours on 
weekdays 
30 - USIU, Mira Mesa, UTC, UCSD on Gilman Drive to 
Downtown via La Jolla and Pacific Beach on weekdays 
34 - UTC, La Jolla Village Square, La Jolla Shores, Pacific 
Beach, MiSsion Beach, Sports Arena, Old Town, Downtown, 
Horton Plaza, Amtrak train station, Greyhound bus station 
41 - VA Hospital to Fashion Valley via Gene$.e8, UTC, University 
City, Clairemont and Unda Vista 
*Free bus rldea around campus and beyond for UCSD students, 
faculty, staff, grad students and spousesl The new expanded 
UCSO free bus zone includes Genesee Ave. to Balboa Ave. and 

the coastal route past downtown La Jolla as far south as Belmont 
Park on Mission Blvd. Just bring your UCSD photo 10 to 
Rideshare Operations at 201 University Center for your free 
yellow bus sticker or call S34-RIDE. 
Traveling beyond the zone? Monthly bus and trolley passes ($39) 
with valid student 10 are at the Cashier's Office, 401 University 
Center. 
Free bus schedules are available at Rideshare Operations or 
RIDESHARE boards throughout campus. 
Need more bus information? Call 233-3004 Monday - Friday S:30 
a.m.- 8:30 p.m.; Sat. & Sun. 8 a.m.-S p.m. Know your bus route 
and stop? Call1nfoExpress at 685-4900 24 hours a day for 
schedule information.

Health Care-
Social Issues 
THE HEALTH CARE·SOCIAL ISSUES PROGRAM offers an interdisciplinary 
minor that offers students a variety of perspectives that enhance the ability to deal 
with complex social and ethical issues in modern health care. The interdisciplinary 
curriculum complements natural science, humanities , and social science major~ 
and enriches students' preparation for professional and postgraduate educat ion 10 
the health care professions. Among the careers students in the program are 
pursuing are medical doctors, registered nurses, physician assistants, physical 
therapists, and osteopathic doctors. Many students go on to schools of public health 
and study biostatistics, community health sciences, environmental hea.lth sciences, 
environmental science and engineering, epidemiology, and health services.

ARENA 
What is your craziest college 

experience? 
Interviews by Jessica Scheppmann 
Photography by Claire Schneider 

When you are a student, sometimes you drink, and I 
was drunk. I can't remember when I fell a leep, but 
when I woke up all my body hair had been shaved off 
and my friends had used white-out to paint on my body. 

Christophe Bourbier 
Revelle EAP 

My friend losh got drunk one night and he locked 
himself into one of the stalls. He was all bent over, and 
I thought he was crying because he looked real sad and 
stuff. I crawled under the stall and was talking to him 
and all of a sudden he opened up his mouth and let 
loose and the puke bounced otf the floor and hit me in 
face. 

Andy Sarouhan 
Marshall Sophomore 

I chased monsoons through the desert, and almost 
got struck by lightning. We were chasing them with 
cars just because my friend was a meteorology student 
and we just wanted to be there . 

• 

Gin Yang 
Muir Senior 

Freshman year, the girls downstairs were getting 
back at us for a prank and so one night they put garbage
